< Review>
This place!!! We absolutely loved it! From the location to the food to the awesome staff! I will start off by saying that I am a very picky person, I am a planner, a worrier, a perfectionist (you get where I am going) - so with that said... I am hard to please, LOL! However, Coffee Cup Cafe far exceeded any expectations I had! It was my birthday weekend (a long bday weekend) and we went down to La Jolla early on a Monday morning with 2 main focuses... The beach and to eat! We found parking right in front and walked inside and were greeted with a big smile and a welcoming vibe! We chose to eat outside and it was just perfect! We got this quaint, local vibe and I loved it! Also, sitting outside you can day dream over the beautiful buildings and their architecture, people watch etc!

Thank you for an unbelievable birthday breakfast!

They serve their food like a work of art!<//Review>

< rating>
5< /rating>
< review>
If you want to avoid the hassle and sit immediately, arrive shortly after they open. By 9 AM there is going to be some wait involved, the bigger the group, the longer the wait.

The food is a hybrid of traditional American with lots of Mexican flair. The chorizo hash browns were incredible. If you order this dish, order a side of toast as it is the one dish that didn't come with bread or tortilla.

The space is cozy and a little tight but the people are friendly and always pleasant. Been here a few times and the staff is super attentive and want to make sure everything is right. They serve Cafe Moto and their french roast is incredibly good. A short walk to the cove in La Jolla makes this spot a great weekend spot to have a great meal and then a walk at beach. It is San Diego and we have quite possibly the best weather in the world. Enjoy!<//review>

< Review>
Coffee Cup is a quaint little breakfast place set in La Jolla. If the place gets busy, I doubt if you can even find a seat, it is that small. The menu is vegetarian friendly and I liked the choice of breakfast items they had. The waitresses were prompt and friendly. However, I really didn't love my food that much. It was a 4 egg white scramble with rice and beans and I found the quantity a tad less and the taste not out of this world. I will reassess my rating after eating again.
Oh, btw, parking is a big pain  in that area. Good luck finding a spot, or else, make sure you have at least 3 dollars in cash for the parking garages.< /Review>

<text>Tajran, Wendy, Hannah, Lucy, the medical team at Sharp Mary Birch, everyone is great!
They all took care of me while I was going through a difficult and high risk pregnancy. It was my first time being pregnant and I had morning sickness throughout the entire time. Wendy was always there to reassure me and tell me stories about her own pregnancies. She was also there to help me when I found out that my pregnancy was high risk and that I would have to be placed on immediate bedrest and then hospitalized at 24 weeks. She helped me access disability for my workplaces (Chula Vista School District and the Corvette Diner) and attain a leave of absence from my school (SDSU). I went from being the busiest girl on earth to living in a hospital and having to press a call button for the smallest things.
However, every day that I was in the hospital, even past delivery, Dr. Tajran checked in on me. She even knitted with me! She always takes the most cautionary measures to make sure you and your child are well. That is her top priority above all else and she will advocate for you. While at the hospital, she told the nurses that I could and should be up ad lib so that I would not have to sit on a bed all day every day. When I was recovering from my C-section, I could hear her advocating for the woman next door. She told the nurses that the woman needs to be able to see her baby ASAP.
I think one thing a lot of people don't realize is that Dr. Tajran is extremely busy. She is always on-call, she checks in with patients at both of her offices/clinics, checks in on each and every high risk pregnant person at Sharp Mary Birch, performs surgeries, helps deliver babies, and checks up on patients postpartum BUT despite all of that, she provides quality care.
Thanks to Dr. Tajran, my baby survived and so did I! He came six weeks early and was 4 pounds 1 oz and needed a bit of help breathing, but other than that he was completely healthy. During the time he was in the NICU, I ran into Hannah who was volunteering to pass out food to families with children at Rady's Children Hospital or in the NICU which was really nice. Out of everyone, Hannah was the most informed and up to date on my care. She made sure that I was going to my NSTs and getting my blood work. If it weren't for her, I might not have known that my pregnancy was so high risk.
Postpartum, Lucy was very helpful in getting me a pump through my insurance so that I could provide for my child while he was in the NICU.
Wendy also tried her best to get me more time at home to bond with my baby postpartum, since he was in the NICU for almost 2 months.

All of this is to say that if you chose Tajran, you are in wonderful hands. I am incredible thankful to her and her staff. I live in Chula Vista and make the drive all the way up to Mira Mesa for quality care and people who advocate for me and my child's needs.</text>< Pictures>

< review>
I am 22 weeks into my second pregnancy. During my first trimester I didn't receive any medical attention by any ob/gyn because I was living out of state when I got pregnant and then when I moved back to San Diego, I had to go on government assistance...which is a joke. At first I had so many issues with the insurance I had and the initial doctor I had chose. I had started bleeding at 12 weeks and couldn't get into an ob for over a month. I eventually changed insurances because it would have been longer. Anyways, long story short, a day after my new insurance was in place i called Dr Tajran's office. She was recommended to me by a coworker, and after explaining my terrible experiences I was seen that same day. Yes the wait was long (i was super early too, so it made the wait longer) and the waiting room eventually got super packed but to me, those are minor issues. They are very thorough and made sure me and baby were ok. I didn't meet the Dr and still havent. I have only seen the nurse practitioner. I see that as some complaints. However, my mom worked ob/gyn as a nurse for many, many years and sometimes patients wont be able to schedule with the dr untill in labor and delivery giving birth lol. To me, the staff seems very nice and I've never had a problem. Not even when I arrived early and had my 2 year old with me. Of course she got restless and whiny towards the end but I was never made to feel like we were unwelcomed. I see it as a full waiting room means lot of people would rather see this Dr. A lot of people come on here to rant about the negative so why not post something positive.</review>

< review>
Service, food and atmosphere was great.

The atmosphere is such that one can feel comfortable dressing up or dressing simply. The service and staff were very friendly and attentive without being bothersome.

I wouldn't call the food exceptional, but it was very, very good.

Every meal comes with soup, salad and bread, all of which are large enough to make a meal on its own.

I had the lasagna which was great, and the wife had the chicken scallopini which she also enjoyed very much.

We also ordered the tomato bruschetta which was nice and fresh and had a nice flavor.

The portions will not leave you wanting more.

Highly recommended for a great Italian meal in the area.< /review>

<review>This place is hit and miss. We waited 8 months after moving here to finally try this place.

First visit was ah-mazing!

Service: We got a great server (who we recognized from 88 burgers next door as she works there as well). She was attentive, knowledgeable, friendly and had hustle.

Food: this too was 5-star. All but the canned vegetable soup served in an outdated Tupperware bowl. The carbonara is delicious... the best I've ever had! Their salads and bread are great too. To end a great dinner we grabbed a cappuccino and cheesecake because we didn't want our great experience to end. We left excited to go back.

Visit 2:
On this night I took my 16-year son and his girlfriend here for dessert. We waited for-ev-er to even get acknowledged once we sat down. The owner lady didnt seem to care that we went for an extended period of time without even so much as a glass of water, instead she sat at the table next to us and started partaking in food and wine with a party of about 8 that was there. I was finally able to order the cappuccino and cheesecake while the teens ordered icecream... this process was painful and I felt frowned upon for only ordering dessert! Awaiting the bill was a process in itself. When we went to pay our server was up there trying to sort out their tickets as they use an archaic paper system for ticketing.
Service: horrible
Food: Great

Final visit:
The husband and I decided again to go for dessert. I wanted the carbonara so bad but pasta hurts my stomach and I can only eat it occasionally. So we went for a mini date night dessert.

I ordered my usual.. the cappuccino and cheesecake. Let me tell you they have the best cheesecake. It is not made in house but it's so good!

Service: The server took her time serving us water I  dirty glasses. When she came she seemed confused that we were only ordering dessert. This is the second time I've felt judged for only order dessert. It's not like people are knocking down the door to get in.  Annoying. But even more annoying is that she couldn't tell us what their $15.00 dessert for two was. When asked she replied, "it's some custard thing"... um... it's a big ticket item on your menu and you dont know? So we ordered my usual and my husband got icecream.

Ugh.

Both our coffees were so gross. My cappuccino was the most vile coffee I've ever had. It was bitter, it was awful. I sent it back and the same exact taste came back with the remake. It's almost like their machine needs to be cleaned, im not sure as I'm no barista. When we left we decided we will never be back.

Its sad.. I want to support local businesses although I feel like if you're not a known local around here with roots they could care less about your business. None the less I love their pasta so I wanted to love this place. It just isnt worth the cost when combined with the inconsistencies and poor service.

I was even willing to look past their outdated decor and dated processes. They do NOT even have beer on tap. We have an AMAZING local brewery (Amador Brew) that should be carried on draft. But they do not have draft beers. Remodel this place, train your employees, and value your customers both new and old. Oh and clean your machines!</review><pics>None< /pics>< gmap_id>

< Review>
Good Vietnamese food.  Prices on the higher side, especially for being in a not great area of town.  $13 bowl of pho, $5.50 for nem nuong coun...

The grilled pork is fantastic and tasty.  Pho wasn't too hot.  Nem nuong coun is solid.

Definitely worth a visit.</Review>

< review>
Very fast service (took them 1 day to replace speakers and radio during the winter holidays) and were extremely kind and generous to me.

Here is a short summary of my experience:

As David, one of the owners, was giving me a tutorial of my new system, my younger brother had noticed that the radio they put in it wasn't the one I brought (I hadn't even looked at the radio I brought as it was a hand-me down from my older brother and didn't see the need to inspect it beforehand).

Turns out there was a misunderstanding and they had installed a new one (and I think a better one) without charging me for it. David said that usually in this situation they'd take the the one I had brought instead as payment, but then said that's not how he does business and told us to keep it. I then offered to leave my car there and have them put in the one we originally brought, but again he turned it down and told me it was a gift for the holidays.

They go above and beyond what you'd expect from a small local shop. If you need car electronics work done, I highly recommend Phantom Electronics. I cannot say enough about how impressed I am with their customer treatment.</review>

<Time>1620092737716< /Time><rating>2<//rating>< Text>
My experience was mediocre at best, with nothing particularly memorable. Despite the fact that the lady at the counter was polite and attentive, my meal did not live up to my standards. When I walk into a restaurant, I expect restaurant-quality food, or at the very least an attempt, but what I got was fast food. I ordered a burrito with just beef, but it didn't say anything about the meat being covered in sauce. I thought I ordered a regular burrito, not a wet one, because I couldn't keep my burrito from turning into a soup due to the amount of liquid that leaked out of it. Worse, it wasn't even properly wrapped, causing it to break almost instantly. It appears that the person who created it lacked care or effort and simply wanted to get it done as soon as possible. I'm disappointed because I wanted something I could eat with my hands rather than with a fork. Overall, I enjoyed the meal, but it appeared to be more of a fast food option than high-quality restaurant fare. It's good, but it doesn't entice me to return.</Text>

<username>Joseph Norman</username>< date>
1539936342081</date>
<rating>5< /rating>< review>
My friend and I were trying to find a cheap place to eat in the area and decided on El Abaje√±o (after seeing its good reviews and convenient location).
Admittedly, when we first arrived, we were a little apprehensive; El Abaje√±o is on the corner of a rather dreary-looking Culver City intersection and shares one of its walls with a 7-11-esque convenience store. However, once we were inside, our apprehensions were happily mistaken.

Aesthetically, the restaurant is very pretty and authentic to traditional Mexican restaurants; the tables are decorated with mosaics, there's artworks across the walls, and the restaurant is painted in an orangey-yellow that allows a lot of light. There's plenty of space in the restaurant, and despite the nearby intersection and outdoor busy street, it is *very* quiet on the inside.
At El Abaje√±o, you order at the front in an assembly-line fashion and (with most of the dishes) by the time you get to the front of the line, your food is ready. Then you sit down! (There's also a cart filled with homemade spicy and mild sauces to add to your meal). My friend (who is vegetarian) ordered a veggie burrito and I (who am not vegetarian) ordered two tacos asadas.
Firstly, the price can not be beat: for my two well-stuffed tacos + complimentary side of tortilla chips, my order was less than $6 (possibly less than $5?).

Secondly, the food is INCREDIBLE. I've previously lived in M√©xico (and visited all sorts of authentic villages/cities across the country) and El Abaje√±o's food is completely on-par with authentic Mexican food. The meat was so tasty and cured wonderfully and all the ingredients felt very fresh and cooked-well. After my two tacos, I was more than stuffed. Additionally (which can sometimes be a stereotypical concern with exotic food establishments), neither my friend nor I got sick afterwards (and we both have sensitive stomachs).
You can't go wrong with El Abaje√±o: the prices and food are incredible, the portions are huge, and the restaurant is pretty and quaint. Leave your apprehensions at the door and you will have a fantastic (and budget-friendly!) Mexican meal.</review>

<UserId.>108838904075535708510<//UserId.>< Rate>
5<//Rate>
< review>
My friend and I were trying to find a cheap place to eat in the area and decided on El Abaje√±o (after seeing its good reviews and convenient location).
Admittedly, when we first arrived, we were a little apprehensive; El Abaje√±o is on the corner of a rather dreary-looking Culver City intersection and shares one of its walls with a 7-11-esque convenience store. However, once we were inside, our apprehensions were happily mistaken.

Aesthetically, the restaurant is very pretty and authentic to traditional Mexican restaurants; the tables are decorated with mosaics, there's artworks across the walls, and the restaurant is painted in an orangey-yellow that allows a lot of light. There's plenty of space in the restaurant, and despite the nearby intersection and outdoor busy street, it is *very* quiet on the inside.
At El Abaje√±o, you order at the front in an assembly-line fashion and (with most of the dishes) by the time you get to the front of the line, your food is ready. Then you sit down! (There's also a cart filled with homemade spicy and mild sauces to add to your meal). My friend (who is vegetarian) ordered a veggie burrito and I (who am not vegetarian) ordered two tacos asadas.
Firstly, the price can not be beat: for my two well-stuffed tacos + complimentary side of tortilla chips, my order was less than $6 (possibly less than $5?).

Secondly, the food is INCREDIBLE. I've previously lived in M√©xico (and visited all sorts of authentic villages/cities across the country) and El Abaje√±o's food is completely on-par with authentic Mexican food. The meat was so tasty and cured wonderfully and all the ingredients felt very fresh and cooked-well. After my two tacos, I was more than stuffed. Additionally (which can sometimes be a stereotypical concern with exotic food establishments), neither my friend nor I got sick afterwards (and we both have sensitive stomachs).
You can't go wrong with El Abaje√±o: the prices and food are incredible, the portions are huge, and the restaurant is pretty and quaint. Leave your apprehensions at the door and you will have a fantastic (and budget-friendly!) Mexican meal.< /review>

<user_id>100582219690018883899</user_id><name>Alec Guinness</name>< resp>
None</resp>
< Text>
There is lots of Mexican food to be found in Los Angeles.  El Abajeno may very well be the best of the lot.

If you want fancy, go somewhere else.  If you want consistently excellent food for a very reasonable price, then this is the place to be.

It is one of those places where you order from the counter.  They put your food together right there in front of you.  Then they hand it to you and you go sit down and enjoy.

What you get looks just like what comes out of the kitchen at a sit-down Mexican restaurant that charges twice as much for the same meal.

What they are lacking in presentation, they more than make up for in quality.  All of their food it top notch.  I've never had a bad meal there.  The refried beans are the best anywhere and the carne asade is really over the top.

Good food.  Big portions.  Great prices.  Homey atmosphere and no tipping.  It doesn't get any better!</Text>

<Time>1546922334675<//Time>< Review>
L O V E !!!  This is my all-time favorite Mexican restaurant. It is in half of a storefront just behind the United Oil station at the corner of Inglewood and Culver.

The food is very reasonably priced, and always delicious. You go through a cafeteria-like line where all food is prepared before you and to your liking. ou then pay and find a seat to enjoy your meal.

There is also a small salsa bar with a few different kinds of sauces plus marinated vegetables, cilantro, onions, etc.  Most of the salsas are hot, so try a little bit of each until you find the one that works for you.

I can't say enough good things about this restaurant. It really is my favorite!< /Review>

< Text>
I and many, many friends have been coming to El Abaje√±o since 1969.  Do you think we might love it..????  You took too long to think, so I'll just tell you that we love it.  The food is awesome, the servers and managing folks are awesome and the beers (good selection, by the way) are priced inexpensively.  I've tried 80% of all the menu items.  Not one complaint from me or friends.  The only mixed feeling I have about posting a positive review is that sometimes the lines can be long and I don't want them to get longer.   If you like Mexican food, you'll LOVE El Abaje√±o.  The best on the Westside and beyond..!!< /Text>
